    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText9006369319873485870" style="display:none">One girl. One camp for delinquents. One hell of a summer.<br /><br />Falice Winters has always been the goody-two shoes. Her twin Arabelle . . . not so much. So what happens when their dad plans to ship Arabelle off to a camp to clean up her act? Well, naturally, Arabelle would find a way out.<br /><br />Her solution? Falice! It was a simple plan: Falice would pretend to be Arabelle and go to the delinquent camp while Arabelle got to have the time of her life with her boyfriend in London.<br /><br />Falice thought her summer was going to consist of sitting on the couch reading novels all day or hanging out with her friends. Never did it cross her mind that she would be pretending to be her sister in a camp of delinquents. But now she’s stuck at a camp all summer where being rude is the new “in.”<br /><br />And everything turns for the worse when someone figures out her secret.<br /><br />Will Falice survive the summer? Or will everyone learn that she’s faking delinquency?</span>

<div id="review_1441149242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441149242" />
    <a title="Amber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45872718-amber"><img alt="Amber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439469658p2/45872718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1441149242?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/45872718-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1441149242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16565773807153038293">Faking Delinquency is definitely a breath of fresh air. From the basic plot line it seems like this book should be bogged down with the cliche. But Ashley writes in such an original and graceful way that the entire story reads like something new. The characters are fantastic, you can't help but be attached to them, and by the time camp is over you're desperate to still continue with them on further journeys.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7746421401821505539" style="display:none">I first read this book a year or two ago on Wattpad. And then I read it again.   <span id="freeText8722029207117509304" style="display:none">Okay, so if yall like this you need to check out <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thebookgeekssite.wordpress.com/">https://thebookgeekssite.wordpress.com/</a> When I first read this book it was on Wattpadd! I recently found out that it has actually been published as a paperback shortly after I finished reading it. Therefore, most of the chapters are off of Wattpadd now.<br /><br />Plot Review: SOOOOOO, I thought Faking Delinquency was a pretty good book. It follows this good girl Falice as she takes the place of her sister Arabella. Arabella was getting ready to be sent of to a delinquency camp, but somehow she managed to convince Falice into taking her place. (I would never do that, and I would hope my sibling would never ask that of me.) That’s just about the only thing I DIDN’T like about this book! The good things outweigh the bad in this case. While Faking Delinquency, Falice meets three people and for the life of me I can’t remember what they’re names are but they’re important! They all have a reason that they come back to the camp over and over. Their stories are really sappy or kind of sad. Anyway, Falice goes in disguise as her sister, but almost the day she gets to the camp she’s found out by a super hot guy! He kind of holds it over her head, but he actually helps her more than anything. They also pull parent trap pranks on the other kids at the camp! I LOVED it! The ending of the book is something that you will see coming from a mile away, but if you don’t mind it then you should really go check it out!<br /><br />MY RATING? 8.5/10 <br /><br />Recommended? Ah, only if you don’t mind knowing what’s going to happen before it happens. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer521778405234809911">ANOTHER GEM FROM ASHLEY WINTERS!<br/>Every author has something that sets them apart, this girl's books are all amazing. She creates real, compelling characters, character development, beautiful relationships, and a story that will be reread for generations. In this particular story, we see a bond between two sisters that is truly beautiful; one takes the punishment so the other can enjoy her summer. Falice develops from a (wimpy) passive young lady to a passionate teenage girl not to be messed with.</span>
  <span id="freeText521778405234809911" style="display:none">ANOTHER GEM FROM ASHLEY WINTERS!<br />Every author has something that sets them apart, this girl's books are all amazing. She creates real, compelling characters, character development, beautiful relationships, and a story that will be reread for generations. In this particular story, we see a bond between two sisters that is truly beautiful; one takes the punishment so the other can enjoy her summer. Falice develops from a (wimpy) passive young lady to a passionate teenage girl not to be messed with. Over the summer we see a slow brewing romance, sweet moments, and relatable occurrences (namely: the peanut butter addiction) I especially appreciate how real this all is. SPOILER: Will's home life.. :( END SPOILER This book deserves to be a New York Times bestseller, I cannot wait to see it on the big screen! </span>

  <span id="freeText14735595659785502519" style="display:none">This is one of the first books I ever read on Wattpad and it has been one of my favorites ever since. I've recommended it to so many of my friends and they've all loved it too. Not only is the author amazing and extremely kind to her fans, but she is just an extremely talented writer as well. Although the book has some cliches (which, let's be honest, we all enjoy when used tastefully in the way she did), she incorporates so many twists and turns that it's impossible to not be hooked on every word. I promise that if you read this book, not only will you not regret it, but you won't be able to put it down until you've completely gotten through the emotional roller coaster that is Faking Delinquency.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445520958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18264342578875609277">I love Faking Delinquency! It's one of my favorite books to read!! The book itself is all around engaging with the most cliche ways. The way humor comes into play makes this story ten times better! I love how the main character is a twin, making it more unique than it already is! I am a twin myself, and I got to say that the author really does a great job in capturing the bond these two twins have. The way Falice is the complete opposite of her twin makes known that twins are not all the same in</span>
  <span id="freeText18264342578875609277" style="display:none">I love Faking Delinquency! It's one of my favorite books to read!! The book itself is all around engaging with the most cliche ways. The way humor comes into play makes this story ten times better! I love how the main character is a twin, making it more unique than it already is! I am a twin myself, and I got to say that the author really does a great job in capturing the bond these two twins have. The way Falice is the complete opposite of her twin makes known that twins are not all the same in personality. I love how Falice makes friends really fast and pushes herself to become stronger in each chapter of the story. Overall, this is an amazing book that every teen and beyond age must read!!!</span>

  <span id="freeText605628870577810850" style="display:none">This is most definitely the most perfect book anyone will ever read, I kid you not. If you're having a bad day, the story of Will and Falice will brighten up your mood without any effort! The things their group gets up to will leave with stitches on your sides because of hysterical laughing and you'll start believing in the authenticity of pinky promises if you didn't before. Most of all <i>Faking Delinquency</i> will have you squealing and smiling like crazy at the moments between the two protagonists. Needless to say Will and Falice are at the top of my OTP list now. I hope that whoever reads this book experiences the same emotions I went through while reading it and can depend on it to cheer them up.</span>

<div id="review_1443886241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1443886241" />
    <a title="Bree" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47458072-bree"><img alt="Bree" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1443886241?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bree" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bree" href="/user/show/47458072-bree">Bree</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1443886241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11922189363965806286">When I first found Faking Delinquency on Wattpad, I was like "meh". Based on the synopsis, the story seemed basic and cliché but I added it to my library, thinking the book would be a light and entertaining read.<br/>It was definitely a great read. The thing about Ashley Winters is that she has a talent for capturing the readers' hearts or with her characters. Will, Falice, Vanessa (oh my goodness, I love Vanessa), Arabelle and Ky were all such lovely people to read about - they were all so likeable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dWhTItdE61Gcee8MUiZNhUY8GOmClXdKgtOvWy0+uwfc/V3wuELWp2ua5zlqKfvC4DgOEkRB+eLfkVXPDaKXmA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rkmFwmU2U54cLeEkZTWxOLYW38KFsyh4IyFav9fg5gwH3IsQCjBuaOvO6RFdOgd/EBLJOUNnptB+Y6Ar93zKkw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
